       <h1 class="page-title">Getting started with Node.js and Bamboo</h1> 
       <article class="content-with-sidebars"> 
        <div class="page-sidebars"> 
         <div class="page-sidebars-wrap"> 
          <div class="page-sidepanel sidepanel-progress-indicator"> 
           <h4>Getting started with Bamboo</h4> 
           <ul> 
            <li class="progress-page-visited"><a href="/bamboo/understanding-the-bamboo-ci-server-289277285.html">Understanding the Bamboo CI Server</a></li> 
            <li class="progress-page-visited"><a href="/bamboo/aws-account-for-bamboo-750395998.html">AWS account for Bamboo</a></li> 
            <li class="progress-page-visited"><a href="/bamboo/getting-started-with-java-and-bamboo-289277286.html">Getting started with Java and Bamboo</a></li>

            <li class="progress-page-visited"><a href="/bamboo/getting-started-with-ruby-and-bamboo-289277291.html">Getting started with Ruby and Bamboo</a></li>

        <div class="conf-macro output-block" data-hasbody="true" data-macro-name="sp-pagelayout"> 
         <p>Node.js is described as:</p> 
         <blockquote> 
          <p>"a platform built on&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://code.google.com/p/v8/">Chrome's JavaScript engine</a>&nbsp;for easily building fast, scalable network applications. Node.js uses an event-driven, non-blocking I/O model that makes it lightweight and efficient, perfect for data-intensive real-time applications that run across distributed devices."&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="http://nodejs.org/">Node.js</a></p> 
         </blockquote> 
         <p>We agree, and bundle a number of tasks with Bamboo to make it&nbsp;easy for you to get continuous integration and deployment for your Node.js projects.&nbsp;You can find the official Node.js documentation&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="http://nodejs.org/documentation/">here</a>.</p> 
         <h2 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Distributions"><span>Distributions</span></h2> 
         <p>Node.js distributions usually come bundled with&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://www.npmjs.org/">npm</a>, a package manager for the platform, which runs from the command line and manages dependencies for your applications.</p> 
         <p>All npm packages contain a file, usually in the project root, called&nbsp;<code>package.json</code>&nbsp;- this file holds metadata relevant to the project.&nbsp;You can find out more about the package.json file&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://www.npmjs.org/doc/files/package.json.html">here</a>.</p> 
         <h2 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-ConfigureyourNode.jsproject"><span> Configure your Node.js project</span></h2> 
         <p>Add the following dependencies (or devDependencies) to the&nbsp;<code>package.json</code>&nbsp;file in your Node.js project. These are required if you want to use the Grunt, Gulp, Bower, Nodeunit or Mocha Test Runner tasks:</p> 
         <p><strong>Grunt</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://npmjs.org/package/grunt">grunt</a>&nbsp;(v0.4 or newer)</li> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://npmjs.org/package/grunt-cli">grunt-cli</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <p><strong>Gulp</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://www.npmjs.org/package/gulp">gulp</a>&nbsp;(v3.3.2 or newer recommended)</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p><strong>Bower</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://www.npmjs.org/package/bower">bower</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <p><strong>Mocha Test Runner</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://npmjs.org/package/mocha">mocha</a></li> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://npmjs.org/package/mocha-bamboo-reporter">mocha-bamboo-reporter</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <p><strong>Nodeunit</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a rel="nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://npmjs.org/package/nodeunit">nodeunit</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>Your package.json file should look something like this:</p> 
         <div class="code-block conf-macro output-block" data-hasbody="true" data-macro-name="sp-macrooverride-plaintextbody-block"> 
          <pre><code class="language-none">...
"devDependencies": {
    ...
    "mocha": "~1.18",
    "mocha-bamboo-reporter": "*",
    ...
    "nodeunit" : "~0.8"
}
"dependencies": {
    ...
    "grunt": "~0.4",
    "grunt-cli": "~0.1",
    ...
    "gulp": "~3.3.2",
    ...
    "bower": "~1.3.12"
}</code></pre> 
         </div> 
         <p>Install the necessary&nbsp;<code>node_modules</code>&nbsp;before executing any of the Node.js tasks, by adding an&nbsp;<a data-macro-name="sp-nobody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npm" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="false">npm</a>&nbsp;task and using the&nbsp;<code>install</code>&nbsp;command.</p> 
         <h2 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Node.jstasks">Node.js tasks</h2> 
         <p>Bamboo ships with specific tasks for Node.js that make it easy to integrate the Node.js platform with Bamboo. You can use these tasks to set up builds for your Node.js project.</p> 
         <p><img width="600" class="confluence-embedded-image" src="/bamboo/files/687213472/687244331/1/1415685711670/BAM57-nodejs-tasks.png"></p> 
         <p>Note that it is possible to execute scripts installed by the&nbsp;<a data-macro-name="sp-nobody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npm" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="false">npm</a> task&nbsp;from the&nbsp;<code>node_modules</code>; however, we recommend that you use the dedicated tasks for executing such scripts, such as&nbsp;Grunt,&nbsp;Mocha or&nbsp;Nodeunit.</p> 
         <p>Install the necessary&nbsp;<code>node_modules</code>&nbsp;before executing any of the Node.js tasks, by adding an <a data-macro-name="sp-nobody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npm" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="false">npm</a> task and using the <code>install</code> command.</p> 
         <p><span class="confluence-anchor-link conf-macro output-inline" id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npm" data-hasbody="false" data-macro-name="anchor"> </span></p> 
         <h3 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npmtask">npm task</h3> 
         <p>The npm&nbsp;task allows you to execute Node Package Manager commands in build plans and deployment projects.&nbsp;To run npm commands, simply enter the command to execute during task configuration:</p> 
         <p><img width="500" class="confluence-embedded-image" src="/bamboo/files/687213472/687244332/1/1415685711885/BAM57-npm-task-config.png"></p> 
         <p>In order to execute npm commands, the&nbsp;Node.js capability&nbsp;must be present on your build agent (see <a data-macro-name="sp-plaintextbody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-capability" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="true">below</a>).</p> 
         <p>Note: since Node.js and npm are distributed together, Bamboo will use the Node.js capability for npm tasks as well. The path will be modified at run time to point to the npm executable.</p> 
         <h3 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Node.jstask">Node.js task</h3> 
         <p>The Node.js task is a general purpose task that can be used to execute Node scripts within Bamboo.</p> 
         <p><img width="500" class="confluence-embedded-image" src="/bamboo/files/687213472/687244330/1/1415685711641/BAM57-nodejs-task-config.png"></p> 
         <p>To run the Node.js task, the&nbsp;Node.js capability&nbsp;must be present on your local or remote agents (see&nbsp;<a data-macro-name="sp-plaintextbody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-capability" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="true">below</a>).</p> 
         <p>Node.js can be used to execute any custom Node.js scripts or applications. To do so, enter the path of the script to execute in the task configuration, and optionally define additional arguments to pass.</p> 
         <p>Note that it is possible to execute scripts installed by the&nbsp;<a data-macro-name="sp-nobody-link" href="#GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-npm" class="conf-macro output-inline" data-hasbody="false">npm</a>&nbsp;task&nbsp;from the&nbsp;<code>node_modules,</code>&nbsp;however we recommend that you use the dedicated tasks for executing such scripts, such as&nbsp;Grunt,&nbsp;Mocha or&nbsp;Nodeunit.</p> 
         <h3 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Mocha"><span>Mocha</span></h3> 
         <p><span>Mocha is a test framework that runs on the Node.js platform.</span></p> 
         <p>You can use the Mocha Test Runner task to run your Mocha tests – it&nbsp;will create an output file named&nbsp;<code>mocha.json</code>.</p> 
         <p>You can configure the task to parse test results after a successful execution. Alternatively, you can add a Mocha Test Parser task to run afterwards to parse the test results.</p> 
         <p>If you don't do a full checkout on each build, make sure you add a task to delete&nbsp;<code>mocha.json</code>&nbsp;<em>before</em>&nbsp;the Mocha Test Runner task. A simple script task that runs&nbsp;<code>rm -f mocha.json</code>&nbsp;should do the trick.</p> 
         <h3 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Grunt"><span>Grunt</span></h3> 
         <p><span>Use the Grunt task to take advantage of the Grunt task runner.</span></p> 
         <h3 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Nodeunit"><span>Nodeunit</span></h3> 
         <p><span>Nodeunit is a tool for&nbsp;defining and running unit tests for Node.js projects.</span></p> 
         <p>Running the Nodeunit task will create test results in JUnit XML format.</p> 
         <p>You can configure the task to parse test results after a successful execution. Alternatively, you can add a following JUnit Parser task to parse the test results.</p> 
         <p><span class="confluence-anchor-link conf-macro output-inline" id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-capability" data-hasbody="false" data-macro-name="anchor"> </span></p> 
         <h2 id="GettingstartedwithNode.jsandBamboo-Node.jscapability">Node.js capability</h2> 
         <p>Bamboo comes with a definition for a new executable capability called Node.js. In order to use the Node.js task (as well as most of the other Node.js tasks in Bamboo), you need this capability to be present on your local or remote agents.</p> 
         <p>The capability can be auto detected on the server side.</p> 
         <p><img width="500" class="confluence-embedded-image" src="/bamboo/files/687213472/687244329/1/1415685711606/BAM57-nodejs-capabilities.png"></p> 
         <p>The&nbsp; <code>NODE_HOME</code> <span>&nbsp;environment variable will instruct Bamboo where to look for Node.js if it is not installed in a typical directory - it should point to the location of the Node.js installation.&nbsp;<span>Bamboo will search the agent's default directories to find the Node.js installation;&nbsp;<span>it will also search in location specified by&nbsp;<code>NODE_HOME</code>.</span> </span> </span></p> 
        </div>
